package app // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/app"

Package app is Formidable's composition root.

It constructs every domain module with its dependencies, exposes the Wails
service list to main.go, and (later) registers the loopback HTTP routes for the
modules that opt into them.

FUNCTIONS

func APIAssetMiddleware(api http.Handler) func(next http.Handler) http.Handler
    APIAssetMiddleware returns a Wails AssetServer middleware that delegates
    `/api/*` requests to the supplied api handler and lets every other path fall
    through to the default asset chain (the embedded Vue dist).

    Why: the slideout's <img src="/api/images/<tpl>/<file>"> needs to be
    fulfilled by the api handler regardless of whether the user has the optional
    internal HTTP server (wiki/api over loopback) running. The asset server is
    always up because the webview itself depends on it, so this middleware gives
    us a consistent transport for the same route shape.

    `api` is allowed to be nil - defensive against composition-root reordering -
    in which case the middleware is a pure pass-through.

    The signature matches Wails' assetserver.Middleware type
    (func(next http.Handler) http.Handler) so it can plug straight into
    application.AssetOptions.Middleware without an adapter.


TYPES

type App struct {
	About         *about.Service
	System        *system.Service
	Config        *config.Service
	Sfr           *sfr.Service
	Journal       *journal.Service
	Csv           *csv.Service
	Template      *template.Service
	Storage       *storage.Service
	Form          *form.Service
	I18n          *i18n.Service
	Dialog        *dialog.Service
	Render        *render.Service
	Nav           *nav.Service
	Wiki          *wiki.Service
	Dataprovider  *dataprovider.Service
	Plugin        *plugin.Service
	Git           *git.Service
	Gigot         *gigot.Service
	Credential    *credential.Service
	Monitor       *monitor.Service
	Stat          *stat.Service
	Query         *query.Service
	Datacore      *datacore.Service
	Expression    *expression.Service
	History       *history.Service
	Integrity     *integrity.Service
	Logging       *logging.Service
	PDF           *pdf.Service
	Manual        *manual.Service
	CodeFormatter *codeformatter.Service
	UpdateCheck   *updatecheck.Service
	Index         *index.Service

	// Has unexported fields.
}

func New(d Deps) (*App, error)

func (a *App) APIHandler() http.Handler
    APIHandler returns the in-process api handler. main.go feeds this into the
    Wails AssetServer middleware so /api/* requests from the in-app webview (the
    slideout's <img src="/api/images/…">, the form view's API field lookups)
    reach the api handler even when the optional wiki/api HTTP server is OFF.

    This is the in-process variant: identity stamping is wired but the
    network-only defenses (LoopbackOnly, RequireOrigin) are NOT. Asset requests
    originate inside the Wails webview itself - RemoteAddr is empty and there is
    no cross-origin browser tab, so the network guards would only ever produce
    false positives here. The loopback HTTP server uses the fully-wrapped
    variant separately.

func (a *App) Logger() *slog.Logger

func (a *App) SetEmit(fn EmitFunc)
    SetEmit installs the transport that journal events (and the log broadcaster)
    flow through. main.go calls this after building the Wails application;
    once installed, every slog record also reaches the frontend as a "log:entry"
    event.

func (a *App) SetWindowOpener(fn func(url string) error)
    SetWindowOpener installs the Wails-aware function used by
    Wiki.OpenInternalWiki to spawn an in-app webview window. main.go calls this
    after the Wails application is built (the application pointer doesn't exist
    when New() runs). Pass nil to disable.

func (a *App) WailsServices() []application.Service
    WailsServices returns the list of services to register on the application
    options. Order is not significant.

type Deps struct {
	AppRoot        string
	Logger         *slog.Logger
	LogBroadcaster *applog.Broadcaster
}

type EmitFunc func(name string, data any)
    EmitFunc bridges journal events to whatever transport the host app uses
    (Wails, stdout, …). main.go installs the Wails-backed implementation via
    App.SetEmit after the Wails app is built.



package log // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/log"

Package log builds the application's structured logger.

The logger always writes to stderr and (by default) tees to
<AppRoot>/formidable.log. The log file is truncated on every New() call,
so each app start begins with a fresh log. Level can be set programmatically via
Options.Level or via the FORMIDABLE_LOG_LEVEL environment variable. File output
can be disabled by setting FORMIDABLE_LOG_FILE to "0", "false", or "off".

FUNCTIONS

func LogPath(opts Options) string
    LogPath returns the resolved log file path for the given options, or "" when
    file output is disabled or AppRoot is empty.


TYPES

type Broadcaster struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Broadcaster owns the ring buffer + emitter hook. It exposes a slog.Handler
    via Handler(); WithAttrs/WithGroup return derived handlers that share the
    same buffer but carry their own context.

func New(opts Options) (*slog.Logger, *Broadcaster)
    New constructs a logger + Broadcaster per the options. Errors opening the
    log file are silently swallowed and the logger falls back to stderr-only
    - file logging must never prevent the application from starting. The
    broadcaster is always returned and captures every record into its in-memory
    ring; pair it with Broadcaster.SetEmitter to fan records out to a UI
    transport.

func NewBroadcaster(capacity int) *Broadcaster

func (b *Broadcaster) Handler() slog.Handler
    Handler returns a fresh slog.Handler bound to this broadcaster.

func (b *Broadcaster) Recent(n int) []Entry
    Recent returns up to n most-recent entries in chronological order. n<=0
    returns everything currently in the ring.

func (b *Broadcaster) SetEmitter(fn EmitFunc)
    SetEmitter installs (or clears) the per-record emit hook. Safe to call from
    any goroutine; existing in-flight Handle calls finish against whichever
    pointer they captured.

type EmitFunc func(e Entry)
    EmitFunc fans an Entry out to whatever transport the host installs
    (typically Wails Events.Emit). Set may be called once after the host's event
    runtime is ready; pre-installation entries are buffered in the ring and
    replayed via Recent() on demand.

type Entry struct {
	Time  time.Time      `json:"time"`
	Level string         `json:"level"`
	Msg   string         `json:"msg"`
	Attrs map[string]any `json:"attrs,omitempty"`
}
    Entry is a flattened slog.Record suitable for transport over Wails events
    / JSON. Attrs is a flat map (groups are joined into dotted keys) so the
    frontend can render without knowing slog internals.

type Options struct {
	// AppRoot is the directory that holds formidable.log when file logging is on.
	// Empty disables file output regardless of UseFile.
	AppRoot string

	// FileName overrides "formidable.log".
	FileName string

	// Level overrides FORMIDABLE_LOG_LEVEL. Accepts debug/info/warn/error.
	// Empty falls through to the env var, then to info.
	Level string

	// UseFile enables file output. Defaults to true. The FORMIDABLE_LOG_FILE
	// env var can force this off ("0", "false", "off").
	UseFile *bool

	// JSON switches to slog's JSONHandler. Default is TextHandler.
	JSON bool
}



package about // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/about"

Package about exposes the application's identity (name, version, tagline,
author) as a small Wails-bindable service. The splash window and any future
"About" UI read from the same source.

CONSTANTS

const (
	Name    = "Formidable"
	Tagline = "A System for Templates and Markdown Forms"
	Author  = "Peter van de Pas"
	Website = "https://formidable.tools"
)
    App identity. Version is a var (not const) so the release workflow can
    inject the tag value at link time via

        -ldflags "-X github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/about.Version=1.2.3"

    Local dev builds keep the "0.1.0" default.


VARIABLES

var Libraries = []Library{
	{ID: "wails", Name: "Wails 3"},
	{ID: "vue", Name: "Vue 3"},
	{ID: "codemirror", Name: "CodeMirror"},
	{ID: "easymde", Name: "EasyMDE"},
	{ID: "raymond", Name: "aymerick/raymond"},
	{ID: "goldmark", Name: "Goldmark"},
	{ID: "chroma", Name: "Chroma"},
	{ID: "picoloom", Name: "picoloom"},
	{ID: "pdfcpu", Name: "pdfcpu"},
	{ID: "gogit", Name: "go-git"},
	{ID: "expr", Name: "expr-lang/expr"},
	{ID: "gopherlua", Name: "gopher-lua"},
	{ID: "vuedraggable", Name: "vuedraggable"},
	{ID: "vuei18n", Name: "vue-i18n"},
	{ID: "datepicker", Name: "@vuepic/vue-datepicker"},
	{ID: "fontawesome", Name: "Font Awesome"},
	{ID: "keyring", Name: "zalando/go-keyring"},
	{ID: "godog", Name: "cucumber/godog"},
	{ID: "uuid", Name: "google/uuid"},
}
    Libraries is the curated list of load-bearing direct dependencies surfaced
    in the About panel. Order is meaningful - items render top-to-bottom as
    listed. Curation rule: direct deps from go.mod and frontend/package.json
    that the app actively uses; transitive deps and build-only tools (vite, tsc,
    prettier) are excluded.

    Adding or removing an entry here MUST be paired with the
    matching i18n description keys: each Library.ID requires a
    `workspace.information.about.thanks.lib.<id>.desc` string in every locale.
    Tests catch a missing/extra ID across locales.

var Version = "0.1.0"

TYPES

type Info struct {
	Name    string `json:"name"`
	Version string `json:"version"`
	Tagline string `json:"tagline"`
	Author  string `json:"author"`
	Website string `json:"website"`
}
    Info is the wire shape returned to the frontend.

type Library struct {
	ID   string `json:"id"`
	Name string `json:"name"`
}
    Library is one entry in the About panel's "Special thanks to" list:
    a canonical project ID and its display name. Descriptions are per-locale and
    live in i18n (workspace.information.about.thanks.lib.{id}.desc) so we don't
    translate product names.

type Service struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Service is the Wails-facing surface. The identity values are compile-time
    constants; the only state is the injected browser opener used by
    OpenWebsite, supplied by the composition root so the module stays free of
    os/exec (same pattern as wiki.Service).

func NewService(openBrowser func(string) error) *Service

func (s *Service) GetInfo() Info

func (s *Service) GetLibraries() []Library
    GetLibraries returns the canonical credits list - the source of truth for
    the About panel's "Special thanks to" section. Frontend renders one row per
    entry and looks up the per-locale description via i18n. Returns a fresh
    slice so the bound caller can't mutate the package-level Libraries.

func (s *Service) OpenWebsite() error
    OpenWebsite asks the host platform's default browser to load the project
    homepage. The opener is platform-specific and lives in the composition root.



package api // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/api"

Package api serves the /api/collections/* JSON endpoints, a peer surface to
the wiki HTML server on the same loopback listener with fully independent read
paths, content types, and shapes.

FUNCTIONS

func NewHandler(dp Provider, st Storage, wr Writer, tpl Templates, stats Stats, qry Query) http.Handler

TYPES

type CountResponse struct {
	Template string `json:"template"`
	Total    int    `json:"total"`
}
    CountResponse is the body of /api/collections/{template}/count.

type Handler struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Handler exposes the /api/* routes; the mux uses fully-qualified paths so no
    StripPrefix is needed.

type Provider interface {
	ListTemplates(ctx context.Context) ([]dataprovider.TemplateSummary, error)
	IsCollectionEnabled(ctx context.Context, template string) bool
	ListCollection(ctx context.Context, template string, opts dataprovider.CollectionListOpts) (*dataprovider.CollectionPage, error)
	CollectionRev(ctx context.Context, template string) (int64, error)
	ResolveCollectionByID(ctx context.Context, template, id string) (*dataprovider.CollectionItem, bool, error)
}
    Provider is the read surface the API needs from the dataprovider.

type Query interface {
	Run(spec query.Spec) (query.Result, error)
}
    Query runs a constrained SELECT (FDRM) over a template's values.

type Stats interface {
	ListObjects(template string) ([]stat.StatObject, error)
	EvaluateObject(template, name string) (*stat.Grid, error)
	EvaluateComposite(template, name string) (*stat.CompositeGrid, error)
	EvaluateDSL(template, dsl string) (*stat.Grid, error)
}
    Stats is the read surface for /api/statistics/*: a template's named objects
    and their evaluated grids.

type Storage interface {
	LoadForm(templateFilename, datafile string) *storage.Form
	OpenImageFile(templateFilename, name string) ([]byte, string, error)
}
    Storage is the bytes-side read surface: a form's meta+data and raw image
    bytes. OpenImageFile returns nil for a missing file so the handler maps it
    to 404 without sniffing the error.

type TemplateRow struct {
	ID   string `json:"id"`   // stem (e.g. "recepten")
	Name string `json:"name"` // display name from yaml `name`, falling back to stem
	Href string `json:"href"` // /api/collections/<id>
}
    TemplateRow is one entry in the /api/collections directory listing.

type Templates interface {
	LoadTemplate(name string) (*template.Template, error)
}
    Templates loads a parsed template, for the design endpoint.

type Writer interface {
	SaveForm(ctx context.Context, templateFilename, datafile string, data map[string]any) storage.SaveResult
	DeleteForm(templateFilename, datafile string) error
}
    Writer is the write side (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE), split from Storage so an
    audit can grep "Writer" to find every write path.

package auth // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/auth"

Package auth scaffolds the request-identity + capability surface that future
versions of Formidable will rely on for distinguishing the trusted in-process
desktop profile from external HTTP callers.

Today the desktop app is the only consumer: the wiki/api HTTP server binds
to 127.0.0.1 and inherits the active profile's identity for every write.
This package's job is to make that boundary explicit in code rather than
convention, so the upcoming subscription model (per- profile API capability
grants) and CLI server mode have a concrete seam to slot into. The Subscription,
SubscriptionResolver, and Server mode pieces are intentionally minimal - they
exist to document the direction, not to ship features.

CONSTANTS

const DesktopFallbackSubject = "<desktop>"
    DesktopFallbackSubject stands in as Identity.Subject when the active profile
    is not (yet) known - e.g. the config has not loaded or the user has not set
    a profile name. Keeps Identity.Valid() true so the write isn't rejected;
    the audit block still gets "Unknown" / the unknown email so attribution is
    visibly unset.


VARIABLES

var (
	// ErrNotImplemented marks future-path stubs (SubscriptionResolver,
	// server-mode features). Callers should surface 501 to the wire.
	ErrNotImplemented = errors.New("auth: not implemented")

	// ErrNoIdentity is returned by IdentityFromContext when no identity
	// has been resolved. Middleware ordering should make this
	// unreachable in practice - kept so handlers can fail closed.
	ErrNoIdentity = errors.New("auth: no identity in context")
)

FUNCTIONS

func LoopbackOnly(next http.Handler) http.Handler
    LoopbackOnly returns a middleware that 403s any request whose RemoteAddr
    isn't an IPv4 or IPv6 loopback address. Defense-in-depth: the wiki listener
    already binds to 127.0.0.1, but if that bind ever drifts (config, reverse
    proxy, tunnel) the handler layer keeps the API closed by default.

func RequireOrigin(allowedOrigins []string) func(http.Handler) http.Handler
    RequireOrigin returns a middleware that gates write methods on the Origin
    (or, fallback, Referer) header matching one of the configured allowlist
    URLs. GET / HEAD / OPTIONS pass through untouched - CSRF only threatens
    state-changing methods, and forcing an Origin on safe reads breaks tooling
    that doesn't set one (curl, scripts).

    allowedOrigins should be the scheme+host[+port] strings that the wiki/API
    server itself serves under (e.g. "http://127.0.0.1:8080"). Empty allowlist
    denies every write - fail-closed by default.

func ResolveIdentity(r Resolver) func(http.Handler) http.Handler
    ResolveIdentity runs the configured Resolver and stuffs the returned
    Identity onto the request context, so downstream handlers (and
    storage.SaveForm via ctx) attribute writes correctly.

    Failure modes:

        ErrNotImplemented → 501 (subscription path not built yet)
        other error       → 403 (resolver rejected the caller)
        !Identity.Valid() → 403 (resolver buggy or token unmapped)

    Fail-closed so a misconfigured resolver can't quietly elevate an
    unauthenticated request.

func WithIdentity(ctx context.Context, id Identity) context.Context
    WithIdentity returns ctx augmented with the given Identity. Middleware calls
    this after the configured Resolver runs so storage.SaveForm can attribute
    the write without consulting a global provider.


TYPES

type DesktopResolver struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    DesktopResolver attributes every request to the active desktop profile.
    Behaviour-equivalent to today's AuthorProvider closure, just promoted into
    an explicit type so the trust boundary is visible.

func NewDesktopResolver(p ProfileProvider) *DesktopResolver

func (d *DesktopResolver) Resolve(_ *http.Request) (Identity, error)

type Identity struct {
	Kind      IdentityKind
	Subject   string
	Name      string
	Email     string
	ProfileID string
}
    Identity is the resolved caller of a request. Carried through ctx so
    storage.SaveForm can attribute writes without a global provider.

    Subject is the stable id (profile name for desktop, subscription id for
    subscription, fixed sentinel for system). Name/Email feed the audit block;
    they default from the owning profile but may differ for system actors (e.g.
    migration jobs).

func IdentityFromContext(ctx context.Context) (Identity, bool)
    IdentityFromContext returns the Identity previously installed by
    WithIdentity. The second return reports presence so callers can fail closed
    when no identity was resolved. nil ctx is tolerated for defensive callers -
    equivalent to a bare context.

func (i Identity) IsZero() bool

func (i Identity) Valid() bool
    Valid returns true when Kind is recognised and Subject is non-empty.
    The middleware uses this to reject malformed Identities before they reach
    storage.

type IdentityKind string
    IdentityKind classifies who is making a request. The zero value ("") means
    "no identity resolved" - handlers should reject writes from a zero-kind
    identity once the middleware is wired.

const (
	KindDesktop      IdentityKind = "desktop"
	KindSubscription IdentityKind = "subscription"
	KindSystem       IdentityKind = "system"
)
type Mode int
    Mode is the deployment posture. Desktop is the only mode that ships today;
    Server is the directive constant for the planned CLI daemon. app.go pins
    this to Desktop and gates server-only paths off it.

const (
	ModeDesktop Mode = iota
	ModeServer
)
func (m Mode) String() string

type ProfileProvider func() (profileID, name, email string)
    ProfileProvider returns the active profile's identity fields. Wired in
    app.go to read from the config manager so a mid-session profile switch is
    picked up live (the closure is re-invoked per resolve).

type Resolver interface {
	Resolve(r *http.Request) (Identity, error)
}
    Resolver maps an incoming HTTP request to a resolved caller Identity.
    Failures surface as errors, never panics, so middleware picks the response
    code.

type Subscription struct {
	ID               string
	ProfileID        string
	AllowedTemplates []string
	AllowedMethods   []string
	TokenHash        string
}
    Subscription is the minimal future capability grant: a profile-bound
    allowlist of templates × methods, authenticated by a bearer-token hash.
    Intentionally light - no rate limits, scoping rules, or revocation flow yet;
    those land with the CLI daemon.

func (s Subscription) Allows(template, method string) bool
    Allows returns true when the subscription's allowlists cover the given
    template stem and HTTP method. Method comparison is case- insensitive so
    callers don't have to normalise.

type SubscriptionResolver struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    SubscriptionResolver is the directive stub for the planned API subscription
    model. Resolve returns ErrNotImplemented unconditionally - we deliberately
    don't even sniff the Authorization header, so the "not built yet" posture is
    unmistakable in traces.

func NewSubscriptionResolver(s SubscriptionStore) *SubscriptionResolver

func (s *SubscriptionResolver) Resolve(_ *http.Request) (Identity, error)

type SubscriptionStore interface {
	FindByToken(tokenHash string) (Subscription, error)
}
    SubscriptionStore is the read surface for matching incoming bearer tokens.



package codeformatter // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/codeformatter"

Package codeformatter is the backend code-format pass the template editor calls
instead of running prettier in the webview. Standalone: no template/pdf/render
imports. The schemas registry is supplied at construction time (composition root
wires pdf.Schemas() in), so codeformatter knows nothing about picoloom keys - it
only knows how to apply a "parent → children" hint set to flat YAML.

VARIABLES

var ErrMalformed = errors.New("codeformatter: source malformed")
    ErrMalformed wraps any parser failure surfaced by a sub-formatter.
    errors.Is(err, ErrMalformed) distinguishes "the source is broken, leave it
    alone" from infrastructure errors.


TYPES

type Lang string

const (
	LangMarkdown Lang = "markdown"
	LangYAML     Lang = "yaml"
	LangLua      Lang = "lua"
)
type Manager struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}

func NewManager(s Schemas) *Manager
    NewManager builds a Manager with the given schema registry. Pass nil for a
    generic formatter with no repair pass (yaml round-trip only).

func (m *Manager) Format(lang, src string) (string, error)
    Format reformats src for the named language. Returned string is the cleaned
    source; err is non-nil only when parsing failed - in that case the returned
    string is still safe to display (whitespace tidy). Unknown lang values fall
    through to tidy.

type Schemas map[string]map[string]bool
    Schemas maps a top-level frontmatter key (the "parent") to the set of child
    key names that belong under it. Used by the markdown formatter's repair pass
    to re-nest children that were authored at the same column as their parent.

type Service struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Service is the Wails-bound surface for the code formatter. One method:
    Format(lang, src). The frontend CodeEditor calls this on its Format button
    instead of running prettier in the webview, so the YAML inside markdown
    frontmatter blocks gets a real parser pass (yaml.v3) and doesn't depend on
    what survived the paste.

func NewService(m *Manager) *Service

func (s *Service) Format(lang, src string) (string, error)
    Format reformats src according to lang. Errors are returned as strings
    via Wails - the frontend toasts ErrMalformed cases so the user can fix the
    source rather than silently shipping broken YAML.



package credential // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/collaboration/credential"

Package credential wraps the OS-native keychain (macOS Keychain / Linux Secret
Service / Windows Credential Manager) via zalando/go-keyring, shared between the
Git and GiGot backends to persist a PAT or token without writing it to disk in
plaintext.

# Account naming convention

All callers must produce keychain account strings of the form:

    <profile_filename>:<backend>:<identifier>

where:
  - profile_filename is the active profile basename; profile namespacing keeps
    "personal" and "work" tokens separate even against the same remote.
  - backend is "git" or "gigot".
  - identifier is per-backend: a remote URL for Git, a repo name for GiGot.

The frontend mirrors this in frontend/src/composables/useCredentialAccount.ts;
keep both definitions aligned if either side changes.

TYPES

type LookupResult struct {
	Found bool `json:"found"`
}
    LookupResult is the Has-query result.

type Manager struct{}
    Manager is the read/write entry point for the OS keychain.

func NewManager() *Manager
    NewManager constructs the credential Manager.

func (m *Manager) Delete(account string) error
    Delete removes the entry for account. Idempotent: deleting a missing entry
    is not an error.

func (m *Manager) Get(account string) (string, error)
    Get returns the secret stored under account. Treat ErrNotFound as "user must
    re-enter the PAT", not fatal.

func (m *Manager) Has(account string) bool
    Has reports whether a non-empty entry exists under account.

func (m *Manager) Set(account, secret string) error
    Set stores secret under the given account name, overwriting any existing
    entry.

type Service struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Service is the Wails-bound surface of the credential Manager.

func NewService(m *Manager) *Service

func (s *Service) Delete(account string) error
    Delete removes the entry for account.

func (s *Service) Has(account string) LookupResult
    Has returns whether a non-empty secret is present for account.

func (s *Service) Set(account, secret string) error
    Set stores secret under account.



package gigot // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/collaboration/gigot"

Package gigot owns the GiGot remote-sync backend, a sibling of the git package
that speaks JSON-over-HTTP to a GiGot server, authenticated by a long-lived
subscription bearer.

The subscription bearer is NOT a git HTTPS PAT (different secret, different
lifecycle; see the credential-separation memory). This is a client, not a
server: the scaffold marker (.formidable/context.json) is written by GiGot at
repo creation.

CONSTANTS

const EventSyncProgress = "gigot:sync_progress"
    EventSyncProgress is the Wails event name the Service emits on progress.

const TrackRecordRel = ".formidable/sync.json"
    TrackRecordRel is the context-relative path of the client-side ledger.


VARIABLES

var (
	// ErrMissingConn fires when an op is invoked without a Connection.
	ErrMissingConn = errors.New("gigot: missing connection")

	// ErrMissingBaseURL fires when a Connection has no BaseURL set.
	ErrMissingBaseURL = errors.New("gigot: missing base url")

	// ErrMissingToken is the pre-flight check for a missing subscription bearer, distinct from a server 401.
	ErrMissingToken = errors.New("gigot: missing subscription token")

	// ErrMissingRepo fires when a repo-scoped op has an empty RepoName.
	ErrMissingRepo = errors.New("gigot: missing repo name")

	// ErrMissingContext fires when an orchestration op has no context folder.
	ErrMissingContext = errors.New("gigot: missing context folder")

	// ErrMissingDestinationID fires when DestinationSync is called without a destination ID.
	ErrMissingDestinationID = errors.New("gigot: missing destination id")

	// ErrEmptyContext fires when the walker finds no Formidable-managed files (likely a misconfigured path).
	ErrEmptyContext = errors.New("gigot: no formidable files in context folder")

	// ErrNoParentVersion fires when the remote repo has no commits yet (gigot returns 409); first-commit path not yet implemented.
	ErrNoParentVersion = errors.New("gigot: remote repo has no HEAD")

	// ErrNotImplemented is the scaffold sentinel; production paths must not return it.
	ErrNotImplemented = errors.New("gigot: not implemented")
)

FUNCTIONS

func AttachProgress(s *Service, emit func(name string, data any))
    AttachProgress installs the emit function for PullLocal/Reclone SyncProgress
    events. Package-level, not a method: the Wails binding generator rejects
    interface-typed params on bound methods (see git.AttachSysgit).

func GitBlobSha(data []byte) string
    GitBlobSha computes a blob's git SHA1: SHA1("blob " + len + "\0" + content),
    matching git's tree-entry hash.

func IsFormidablePath(repoRelPath string) bool
    IsFormidablePath reports whether a repo-relative path is Formidable-managed
    (templates/, storage/, or an allowlisted root file). Rejects ".." traversal
    so callers can pass server tree paths without re-validating.

func TrackRecordPath(contextFolder string) string
    TrackRecordPath returns the absolute path of the client-side ledger for a
    context folder.


TYPES

type Author struct {
	Name  string
	Email string
}
    Author identifies who made a commit; empty fields are dropped at encode time
    to pass server validation.

type Change struct {
	Op         string `json:"op"`
	Path       string `json:"path"`
	ContentB64 string `json:"content_b64,omitempty"`
	Blob       string `json:"blob,omitempty"`
}
    Change is one put/delete op; ContentB64 is required for put, and Blob is set
    on the response side after the server hashes post-merge content.

type ChangeFile struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Status string `json:"status"`
}
    ChangeFile is one per-path entry in a commit's changes list; Status is a
    single-letter code A/M/D/R.

type CommitRequest struct {
	ParentVersion string   `json:"parent_version"`
	Changes       []Change `json:"changes"`
	Message       string   `json:"message"`
	Author        *Author  `json:"author,omitempty"`
}
    CommitRequest is the body of POST /api/repos/{repo}/commits; ParentVersion
    must equal HEAD or the server returns 409.

type CommitResponse struct {
	Version string   `json:"version"`
	Changes []Change `json:"changes,omitempty"`
}
    CommitResponse: Version is the new HEAD; Changes echoes the post-merge
    content the server wrote (differs from what we sent on F1 auto-merge).

type ConfigReader interface {
	GigotBaseURL() string
	GigotRepoName() string
	AuthorName() string
	AuthorEmail() string
	ContextFolder() string
}
    ConfigReader yields the gigot fields off the active profile; empty Author
    makes the server use the subscription's default identity.

type Connection struct {
	BaseURL  string
	Token    string
	RepoName string
	Author   *Author
}
    Connection is the per-call addressing + auth bundle for any HTTP op;
    Token is the GiGot subscription bearer. A populated Author becomes the git
    author on commits, so the audit trail shows the team member, not the service
    account.

type CredentialReader interface {
	Get(account string) (string, error)
}
    CredentialReader resolves the GiGot subscription bearer (NOT a git PAT) for
    a keychain account; empty + nil means "no entry".

type Destination struct {
	ID             string `json:"id"`
	Name           string `json:"name"`
	URL            string `json:"url"`
	Auto           bool   `json:"auto"`
	LastSyncStatus string `json:"last_sync_status,omitempty"`
	LastSyncAt     string `json:"last_sync_at,omitempty"`
	LastSyncError  string `json:"last_sync_error,omitempty"`
	RemoteStatus   string `json:"remote_status,omitempty"`
}
    Destination is one mirror-sync target; RemoteStatus is the server's
    mirror view: "in_sync", "diverged", "error", or empty (never checked /
    invalidated).

type DiffResult struct {
	Changed []LocalFile
	Deleted []string
}
    DiffResult holds files whose SHA changed (Changed) and managed paths the
    ledger remembers but disk lost (Deleted).

func DiffAgainstRecord(local []LocalFile, rec TrackRecord) DiffResult
    DiffAgainstRecord compares the walker output to the track-record. On first
    sync (rec.Version empty) Deleted is suppressed: the seeded ledger holds
    every server path and we must not nuke content pull will fetch next.

type FileResponse struct {
	Path       string `json:"path"`
	ContentB64 string `json:"content_b64"`
	Blob       string `json:"blob,omitempty"`
	Size       int64  `json:"size,omitempty"`
}
    FileResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/repos/{repo}/files/{path};
    ContentB64 is the base64-std raw blob.

type Filesystem interface {
	SaveFile(path string, content string) error
}
    Filesystem is the atomic-write surface Manager needs: SaveFile is
    temp+fsync+rename, so a crash never leaves a partial sync.json.

type FormidableMarkerView struct {
	Version      int    `json:"version"`
	ScaffoldedBy string `json:"scaffolded_by,omitempty"`
	ScaffoldedAt string `json:"scaffolded_at,omitempty"`
}
    FormidableMarkerView mirrors gigot's marker payload, letting the client
    detect scaffold-version mismatches.

type FormidableStorage struct {
	Template string `json:"template"`
	Files    int    `json:"files"`
}
    FormidableStorage is one storage/ template dir; Files counts .meta.json
    records only (images/ excluded).

type FormidableTemplate struct {
	Name string `json:"name"`
	Path string `json:"path"`
}
    FormidableTemplate is one templates/ entry at HEAD; Path is repo-relative
    for /files/{path} fetches.

type HTTPError struct {
	Status int
	Method string
	Path   string
	Body   string
}
    HTTPError wraps a non-2xx gigot response. It carries (not wraps) the route
    so errors.Is sentinels still match.

func (e *HTTPError) Error() string

type HeadResponse struct {
	Version       string `json:"version"`
	DefaultBranch string `json:"default_branch,omitempty"`
}
    HeadResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/repos/{repo}/head; Version is
    the parent_version for the next commit.

type HealthResponse struct {
	OK      bool   `json:"ok"`
	Version string `json:"version,omitempty"`
}
    HealthResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/health.

type LedgerSummary struct {
	Version  string   `json:"version"`
	LastSync string   `json:"lastSync"`
	Changed  []string `json:"changed"`
	Deleted  []string `json:"deleted"`
	Scanned  int      `json:"scanned"`
}
    LedgerSummary is a purely-local snapshot of the ledger + on-disk diff (no
    HTTP) for the Sync UI's pending-state hints.

type LocalFile struct {
	Path  string
	Bytes []byte
	Sha   string
}
    LocalFile is one context-folder walker entry: repo-relative path, on-disk
    bytes, and precomputed git blob SHA.

func CollectFormidableFiles(contextFolder string) ([]LocalFile, error)
    CollectFormidableFiles returns every managed file (templates/ flat *.yaml,
    storage/ recursive, allowlisted root files), each with its bytes + git blob
    SHA.

type LogEntry struct {
	Hash    string       `json:"hash"`
	Parents []string     `json:"parents,omitempty"`
	Refs    []string     `json:"refs,omitempty"`
	Author  string       `json:"author"`
	Email   string       `json:"email,omitempty"`
	Date    string       `json:"date"`
	Message string       `json:"message"`
	Changes []ChangeFile `json:"changes,omitempty"`
}
    LogEntry is one RepoLogResponse row; Changes is populated only when Log is
    called with withChanges=true.

type Manager struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Manager is the transport-neutral gigot backend; HTTP methods take an
    explicit Connection so callers swap servers/tokens without re-init.

func NewManager(fs Filesystem, opts ...ManagerOption) *Manager
    NewManager builds a Manager bound to fs (required: ledger writes always go
    through it for atomicity).

func (m *Manager) Commit(conn Connection, req CommitRequest) (*CommitResponse, error)
    Commit issues POST /api/repos/{repo}/commits (atomic multi-file);
    a ParentVersion that doesn't match HEAD returns 409 (as *HTTPError).

func (m *Manager) Context(conn Connection) (*RepoContextResponse, error)
    Context issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/context.

func (m *Manager) DestinationSync(conn Connection, destinationID string) (*Destination, error)
    DestinationSync issues POST /api/repos/{repo}/destinations/{id}/sync (manual
    mirror-push retry, synchronous server-side).

func (m *Manager) Destinations(conn Connection) ([]Destination, error)
    Destinations issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/destinations, unwrapping the
    server's {destinations, count} envelope to a slice.

func (m *Manager) Formidable(conn Connection) (*RepoFormidableResponse, error)
    Formidable issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/formidable (marker + templates +
    storage summary).

func (m *Manager) GetFile(conn Connection, repoRelPath string) (*FileResponse, error)
    GetFile issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/files/{path}; encodeSegments preserves
    slashes while URL-encoding each segment.

func (m *Manager) Head(conn Connection) (*HeadResponse, error)
    Head issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/head; an empty repo returns 409 (as
    *HTTPError) so the first-write path can detect "no HEAD yet".

func (m *Manager) LedgerSummary(contextFolder string) (*LedgerSummary, error)
    LedgerSummary diffs the context folder against the ledger for the Sync UI;
    read-only, never writes the ledger.

func (m *Manager) Log(conn Connection, limit int, withChanges bool) (*RepoLogResponse, error)
    Log issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/log[?limit=N&with_changes=1]; limit<=0
    omits the query (server default page size).

func (m *Manager) Me(conn Connection) (*MeResponse, error)
    Me issues GET /api/me (bearer-aware, repo-agnostic).

func (m *Manager) Ping(conn Connection) (*HealthResponse, error)
    Ping issues GET /api/health; tolerates a missing RepoName (repo-agnostic).

func (m *Manager) PullLocal(conn Connection, contextFolder string) (*PullResult, error)
    PullLocal fetches the server tree and writes any blob whose local SHA
    differs, deleting vanished managed paths. The ledger is rebuilt from the
    authoritative tree, so the server wins any disagreement.

func (m *Manager) PullLocalWithProgress(conn Connection, contextFolder string, cb ProgressFunc) (*PullResult, error)
    PullLocalWithProgress is the progress-instrumented PullLocal, emitting
    Start, Tree, Delete, Fetch, Done events; nil cb degrades to PullLocal.

func (m *Manager) PushLocal(conn Connection, contextFolder string, message string) (*PushResult, error)
    PushLocal walks the context folder, diffs against the track-record,
    and commits changed files. On first sync (no ledger) it seeds from /tree so
    we don't blindly re-push files the remote already has. Blob SHAs come from
    raw bytes via GitBlobSha; no .git/ is touched.

func (m *Manager) ReadTrackRecord(contextFolder string) TrackRecord
    ReadTrackRecord loads the ledger at contextFolder, returning
    EmptyTrackRecord (no error) when missing/corrupt so a fresh checkout doesn't
    break sync.

func (m *Manager) Reclone(conn Connection, contextFolder string) (*PullResult, error)
    Reclone wipes every gigot-managed path then pulls fresh from the server.
    Local-only edits in managed paths are LOST by design; non-managed files are
    preserved.

func (m *Manager) RecloneWithProgress(conn Connection, contextFolder string, cb ProgressFunc) (*PullResult, error)
    RecloneWithProgress is the progress-instrumented Reclone, emitting PhaseWipe
    before the destructive sweep then delegating to PullLocalWithProgress.

func (m *Manager) Sync(conn Connection, contextFolder string, message string) (*SyncResult, error)
    Sync runs PushLocal then PullLocal; a push error aborts before pull so
    unpushed local changes aren't overwritten.

func (m *Manager) Tree(conn Connection) (*TreeResponse, error)
    Tree issues GET /api/repos/{repo}/tree (recursive file listing at HEAD).

func (m *Manager) WriteTrackRecord(contextFolder string, rec TrackRecord) error
    WriteTrackRecord persists the ledger to <context>/.formidable/sync.json via
    the atomic-write Filesystem, pretty-printed for diffability.

type ManagerOption func(*Manager)
    ManagerOption configures a Manager at construction time.

func WithHTTPClient(c *http.Client) ManagerOption
    WithHTTPClient swaps the default http.Client.

type MeResponse struct {
	User         User         `json:"user"`
	Subscription Subscription `json:"subscription"`
}
    MeResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/me.

type ProfileReader interface {
	CurrentProfileFilename() string
}
    ProfileReader yields the active profile filename; "" disables keychain
    auto-resolve.

type ProgressFunc func(SyncProgress)
    ProgressFunc is the progress callback; the Manager calls it inline between
    HTTP requests, so it must NOT block.

type PullResult struct {
	Version string `json:"version"`
	Files   int    `json:"files"`
	Deleted int    `json:"deleted"`
}
    PullResult is PullLocal's success envelope: tree version, files written,
    files removed.

type PushResult struct {
	Version string `json:"version"`
	Pushed  int    `json:"pushed"`
	Deleted int    `json:"deleted"`
	Scanned int    `json:"scanned"`
	Noop    bool   `json:"noop"`
}
    PushResult is PushLocal's success envelope; Noop means no bytes moved.

type RepoContext struct {
	Head             string `json:"head,omitempty"`
	DefaultBranch    string `json:"default_branch,omitempty"`
	Empty            bool   `json:"empty"`
	IsFormidable     bool   `json:"is_formidable"`
	DestinationCount int    `json:"destination_count"`
}
    RepoContext is the repo-side half of /context; IsFormidable is set when the
    server finds a .formidable/context.json marker.

type RepoContextResponse struct {
	User         User         `json:"user"`
	Subscription Subscription `json:"subscription"`
	Repo         RepoContext  `json:"repo"`
}
    RepoContextResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/repos/{repo}/context.

type RepoFormidableResponse struct {
	MarkerPresent bool                  `json:"marker_present"`
	Marker        *FormidableMarkerView `json:"marker,omitempty"`
	Templates     []FormidableTemplate  `json:"templates"`
	Storage       []FormidableStorage   `json:"storage"`
}
    RepoFormidableResponse mirrors gigot's server type at
    internal/server/handler_repo_formidable.go; align field-for-field.

type RepoLogResponse struct {
	Name    string     `json:"name"`
	Entries []LogEntry `json:"entries"`
	Count   int        `json:"count"`
}
    RepoLogResponse is the wrapped body of GET /api/repos/{repo}/log; the commit
    trail is in Entries.

type Service struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Service is the Wails-bound surface of the gigot backend. It builds each
    Connection from the active profile + keychain subscription bearer and
    records journal hops on success.

    The subscription bearer never crosses the Wails bridge: the Service is the
    only layer that reads it, keeping Manager transport-neutral.

func NewService(m *Manager, creds CredentialReader, profile ProfileReader, cfg ConfigReader, jrnl journal.Journal) *Service
    NewService wires the gigot Service; any of creds/profile/cfg/jrnl may be nil
    (missing deps surface a config error or skip the journal hop).

func (s *Service) Context() (*RepoContextResponse, error)

func (s *Service) DestinationSync(destinationID string) (*Destination, error)

func (s *Service) Destinations() ([]Destination, error)

func (s *Service) Formidable() (*RepoFormidableResponse, error)

func (s *Service) GetFile(repoRelPath string) (*FileResponse, error)

func (s *Service) Head() (*HeadResponse, error)

func (s *Service) LedgerSummary() (*LedgerSummary, error)
    LedgerSummary previews the ledger + pending diff with no HTTP, driving the
    Sync UI's "what would push/pull do" hints.

func (s *Service) Log(limit int, withChanges bool) (*RepoLogResponse, error)

func (s *Service) Me() (*MeResponse, error)

func (s *Service) Ping() (*HealthResponse, error)

func (s *Service) PullLocal() (*PullResult, error)
    PullLocal fetches the server tree and writes changed files, emitting
    SyncProgress events and recording remote-seen on success.

func (s *Service) PushLocal(message string) (*PushResult, error)
    PushLocal commits changed files in the active context folder, recording a
    journal sync entry on success.

func (s *Service) Reclone() (*PullResult, error)
    Reclone wipes managed paths in the active context folder and pulls fresh;
    destructive (local-only edits dropped), records remote-seen on success.

func (s *Service) Sync(message string) (*SyncResult, error)
    Sync runs PushLocal then PullLocal at the Service layer so each half records
    its own journal entry; a push failure aborts before pull.

func (s *Service) Tree() (*TreeResponse, error)

type Subscription struct {
	Repo      string   `json:"repo"`
	Abilities []string `json:"abilities,omitempty"`
}
    Subscription is the per-token capability bundle, mirroring gigot's
    TokenEntry.

type SyncPhase string
    SyncPhase enumerates the named steps PullLocal / Reclone emit, in order.

const (
	// PhaseStart fires once at entry, before any HTTP (Total is 0, not yet known).
	PhaseStart SyncPhase = "start"
	// PhaseWipe fires before Reclone's local wipe; plain PullLocal never emits it.
	PhaseWipe SyncPhase = "wipe"
	// PhaseTree fires after /tree returns; Total is pending deletes + managed entries.
	PhaseTree SyncPhase = "tree"
	// PhaseDelete fires once per locally-deleted path.
	PhaseDelete SyncPhase = "delete"
	// PhaseFetch fires once per managed entry inspected, even when a SHA-match short-circuits the download.
	PhaseFetch SyncPhase = "fetch"
	// PhaseDone fires once at completion (Current==Total).
	PhaseDone SyncPhase = "done"
)
type SyncProgress struct {
	Phase   SyncPhase `json:"phase"`
	Current int       `json:"current"`
	Total   int       `json:"total"`
	Path    string    `json:"path,omitempty"`
}
    SyncProgress is the payload for gigot:sync_progress events; Path is set only
    on per-file phases (delete/fetch).

type SyncResult struct {
	Version       string `json:"version"`
	Pushed        int    `json:"pushed"`
	PushedDeleted int    `json:"pushedDeleted"`
	Pulled        int    `json:"pulled"`
	PulledDeleted int    `json:"pulledDeleted"`
	Noop          bool   `json:"noop"`
}
    SyncResult is Sync's combined push+pull outcome; Noop is true only when both
    halves were quiet.

type TrackRecord struct {
	Version  string            `json:"version,omitempty"`
	LastSync string            `json:"lastSync,omitempty"`
	Files    map[string]string `json:"files"`
}
    TrackRecord is the client-side ledger at <context>/.formidable/sync.json:
    the last agreed server version plus each managed file's blob SHA. Each team
    member keeps their own copy; deliberately not shared.

func EmptyTrackRecord() TrackRecord
    EmptyTrackRecord returns a zero-value track record with a non-nil Files map.

func ReadTrackRecord(contextFolder string) TrackRecord
    ReadTrackRecord is the package-level form for callers that don't hold a
    Manager.

type TreeEntry struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
	Blob string `json:"blob"`
	Size int64  `json:"size,omitempty"`
}
    TreeEntry is one blob in the tree response; Blob is the git blob SHA1
    matching GitBlobSha.

type TreeResponse struct {
	Version string      `json:"version"`
	Files   []TreeEntry `json:"files"`
}
    TreeResponse is the parsed body of GET /api/repos/{repo}/tree: a recursive
    snapshot at Version (paths + SHAs, no content).

type User struct {
	Username string `json:"username"`
	Provider string `json:"provider,omitempty"`
	Role     string `json:"role,omitempty"`
}
    User identifies the gigot-side account a token belongs to.



package git // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/collaboration/git"

Package git owns the Git collaboration backend. Pure go-git by default (no
system git needed); self-cloned mode shells out to system git so the user's
credential helper handles auth.

FUNCTIONS

func AttachSysgit(s *Service, flags FlagReader, runner Sysgit)
    AttachSysgit enables the self-cloned transport: when GitSelfCloned() is
    true, Fetch/Push/Pull shell out to system git so the user's credential
    helper handles auth. Nil args keep the go-git fallback.

    Package-level, not a method: the Wails binding generator rejects
    interface-typed params on bound methods, and a *Service return would double
    Service as both service and model in the generated index.ts.


TYPES

type Branches struct {
	// Current is the active branch, "" when detached.
	Current string   `json:"current"`
	Locals  []string `json:"locals"`
}
    Branches summarizes local branches plus the active one.

type ChangeFile struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Status string `json:"status"`
}
    ChangeFile is one CommitChanges row; Status is a single-letter code A/M/D/R
    (R is exact-content rename only).

type CloneOptions struct {
	URL    string `json:"url"`
	Dest   string `json:"dest"`
	Branch string `json:"branch"`
	PAT    string `json:"pat"`
}
    CloneOptions describes a clone request. URL and Dest are required;
    empty Branch uses remote HEAD. PAT is the HTTP Basic password (username
    "x-access-token"); empty means anonymous. PAT is transient: never persisted
    by the manager, discarded by the frontend once the response returns.

type CloneResult struct {
	Dest   string `json:"dest"`
	Head   string `json:"head"`
	Branch string `json:"branch"`
}
    CloneResult is the success envelope: worktree, HEAD commit, and branch
    (empty on a detached-HEAD clone).

type Commit struct {
	Hash    string `json:"hash"`
	Short   string `json:"short"`
	Author  string `json:"author"`
	Email   string `json:"email"`
	Time    string `json:"time"`
	Subject string `json:"subject"`
}
    Commit is a JSON-friendly view of a git commit; Time is RFC3339 in the
    author's stored offset.

type CommitOptions struct {
	Path    string `json:"path"`
	Message string `json:"message"`
	Author  string `json:"author"`
	Email   string `json:"email"`
}
    CommitOptions describes a commit request; it stages every worktree change
    before committing.

type CommitResult struct {
	Hash  string `json:"hash"`
	Short string `json:"short"`
}
    CommitResult is the success envelope: the new commit's full hash plus a
    7-char short form.

type CredentialReader interface {
	Get(account string) (string, error)
}
    CredentialReader resolves a stored secret for an HTTPS auth account.
    Empty string + nil error means "no entry", treated as an anonymous attempt.

type DiscardOptions struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
	File string `json:"file"`
}
    DiscardOptions targets a single worktree file to discard its local change.
    File is worktree-relative; path-traversal segments ("..") are rejected.

type FetchOptions struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Remote string `json:"remote"`
	PAT    string `json:"pat"`
}
    FetchOptions describes a fetch request; empty Remote defaults to "origin",
    PAT is transient (see CloneOptions).

type FetchResult struct {
	AlreadyUpToDate bool `json:"already_up_to_date"`
}
    FetchResult signals whether the remote-tracking refs moved.

type FlagReader interface {
	GitSelfCloned() bool
}
    FlagReader exposes per-profile toggles that affect transport selection.

type GraphCommit struct {
	Hash    string   `json:"hash"`
	Short   string   `json:"short"`
	Author  string   `json:"author"`
	Email   string   `json:"email"`
	Time    string   `json:"time"`
	Subject string   `json:"subject"`
	Parents []string `json:"parents"`
	Refs    []string `json:"refs"`
}
    GraphCommit is a Commit enriched with parent hashes (graph edges) and Refs
    (branch tips plus "HEAD") at this commit.

type Manager struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}

func NewManager() *Manager

func (m *Manager) Branches(path string) (*Branches, error)
    Branches lists local branches plus the active one, sorted.

func (m *Manager) Clone(opts CloneOptions) (*CloneResult, error)
    Clone fetches a remote into opts.Dest. opts.PAT enables HTTP basic auth
    (transient, never persisted). Refuses to clone into an existing non-empty
    directory.

func (m *Manager) Commit(opts CommitOptions) (*CommitResult, error)
    Commit stages every worktree change and commits on the current branch.
    Refuses on empty message/author/email, a clean worktree, or a detached HEAD.

func (m *Manager) CommitChanges(path, hash string) ([]ChangeFile, error)
    CommitChanges returns the file-level diff (status A/M/D/R) between the
    named commit and its first parent. Root commits treat every file as added;
    merge commits diff against the first parent, matching `git show`.

func (m *Manager) Discard(opts DiscardOptions) error
    Discard throws away the local change to a single file:

      - tracked + modified/deleted: restore worktree from HEAD blob, re-add to
        refresh the index.
      - staged add or untracked (not in HEAD): remove from index and/or
        worktree.

    Path-traversal segments ("..") are rejected up-front. A missing file is not
    an error: the end state is already "discarded".

func (m *Manager) Fetch(opts FetchOptions) (*FetchResult, error)
    Fetch updates the remote-tracking refs for the remote (default "origin")
    without touching the worktree.

func (m *Manager) IsGitRepo(path string) bool
    IsGitRepo reports whether <path> sits inside a git worktree.

func (m *Manager) Log(path string, limit int) ([]Commit, error)
    Log returns up to <limit> commits walking back from HEAD newest first;
    limit <= 0 means all.

func (m *Manager) LogGraph(path string, limit int) ([]GraphCommit, error)
    LogGraph returns Log's commits enriched with parent hashes and the
    branch/HEAD refs pointing at each.

func (m *Manager) Pull(opts PullOptions) (*PullResult, error)
    Pull fetches the remote (default "origin") and merges upstream into the
    current branch; refuses on detached HEAD. Empty PAT means anonymous.

func (m *Manager) PullWithStash(opts PullWithStashOptions) (*StashedPullResult, error)
    PullWithStash does a journal-aware auto-stash + pull + restore. The pending
    manifest is the authoritative set of files Formidable touched since the last
    sync, narrower than `git status` which would also catch external edits we
    don't own.

    Flow:
     1. Snapshot each pending file into <repoRoot>/.changes.stash/ and capture
        its pre-pull HEAD blob hash.
     2. Reset those paths to HEAD so the worktree is clean and pull can
        fast-forward.
     3. Run the normal Pull.
     4. Per snapshot: post-pull HEAD blob hash differs from pre-pull means the
        file moved under us (conflict); else restore the stash.
     5. Clean restore removes the stash dir; conflicts leave it for manual
        recovery.

    On pull failure the reset paths stay reset and the stash dir remains for
    manual recovery.

func (m *Manager) Push(opts PushOptions) (*PushResult, error)
    Push sends the current branch HEAD to the remote (default "origin");
    refuses on detached HEAD. Empty PAT means anonymous; private HTTPS pushes
    then surface a 401 to the caller.

func (m *Manager) RemoteInfo(path string) (*RemoteInfo, error)
    RemoteInfo returns the configured remotes and their URLs, sorted by name.

func (m *Manager) RepoRoot(path string) (string, error)
    RepoRoot returns the absolute worktree root for <path>.

func (m *Manager) Status(path string) (*Status, error)
    Status snapshots the repo's current branch + worktree state into named
    buckets. A file modified in both index and worktree appears in both Staged
    and Modified, as porcelain does.

func (m *Manager) WithLogger(log *slog.Logger) *Manager
    WithLogger swaps the Manager's logger so open/auth failures reach the in-app
    log (Windows has no devtools).

type OverriddenPath struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Author string `json:"author"`
	Email  string `json:"email"`
	Time   string `json:"time"`
	Commit string `json:"commit"`
}
    OverriddenPath names a path where the local change was dropped for pull's
    content, plus the remote commit's authorship.

type ProfileReader interface {
	CurrentProfileFilename() string
}
    ProfileReader yields the active profile filename. Returning "" disables
    keychain auto-resolve.

type PullOptions struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Remote string `json:"remote"`
	PAT    string `json:"pat"`
}
    PullOptions describes a pull (fetch + merge, no rebase); empty Remote
    defaults to "origin", PAT is transient.

type PullResult struct {
	AlreadyUpToDate bool   `json:"already_up_to_date"`
	NewHead         string `json:"new_head"`
}
    PullResult: NewHead is the post-pull local HEAD hash, recorded as the
    journal cursor version.

type PullWithStashOptions struct {
	PullOptions
	Pending []StashPathPending `json:"pending"`
}
    PullWithStashOptions extends PullOptions with the journal-derived stash
    manifest of dirty-since-sync paths.

type PushOptions struct {
	Path   string `json:"path"`
	Remote string `json:"remote"`
	PAT    string `json:"pat"`
}
    PushOptions describes a push of the current branch HEAD; empty Remote
    defaults to "origin", PAT is transient.

type PushResult struct {
	AlreadyUpToDate bool   `json:"already_up_to_date"`
	NewHead         string `json:"new_head"`
}
    PushResult: NewHead is the local HEAD hash now on the remote, recorded as
    the post-sync cursor version.

type Remote struct {
	Name string   `json:"name"`
	URLs []string `json:"urls"`
}
    Remote is one configured remote with all its push/fetch URLs.

type RemoteInfo struct {
	Remotes []Remote `json:"remotes"`
}
    RemoteInfo wraps the configured remotes for the repo.

type Service struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Service is the Wails-bound surface of the Git backend. It auto-resolves a
    missing PAT from the keychain and records journal sync hops on success.

    The PAT never round-trips through the Wails bridge: the Service is the only
    layer allowed to read it, keeping Manager transport-neutral and unaware of
    credential storage.

func NewService(m *Manager, creds CredentialReader, profile ProfileReader, jrnl journal.Journal) *Service

func (s *Service) Branches(path string) (*Branches, error)

func (s *Service) Clone(opts CloneOptions) (*CloneResult, error)

func (s *Service) Commit(opts CommitOptions) (*CommitResult, error)

func (s *Service) CommitChanges(path, hash string) ([]ChangeFile, error)

func (s *Service) Discard(opts DiscardOptions) error

func (s *Service) Fetch(opts FetchOptions) (*FetchResult, error)
    Fetch refreshes remote-tracking refs via sysgit (credential helper resolves
    auth) or go-git with keychain PAT.

func (s *Service) IsGitRepo(path string) bool

func (s *Service) Log(path string, limit int) ([]Commit, error)

func (s *Service) LogGraph(path string, limit int) ([]GraphCommit, error)

func (s *Service) Pull(opts PullOptions) (*PullResult, error)
    Pull fetches + merges the upstream branch via sysgit or go-git, recording
    remote-seen on success.

func (s *Service) PullWithStash(opts PullOptions) (*StashedPullResult, error)
    PullWithStash is the journal-aware auto-stash variant of Pull. The pending
    set is narrower than `git status` (only journal-dirty paths), so external
    edits don't get stashed; no pending degrades to a plain pull.

func (s *Service) Push(opts PushOptions) (*PushResult, error)
    Push sends commits to the remote; AlreadyUpToDate records remote-seen,
    advancing records a sync marker.

func (s *Service) RemoteInfo(path string) (*RemoteInfo, error)

func (s *Service) RepoRoot(path string) (string, error)

func (s *Service) Status(path string) (*Status, error)

type StashEntry struct {
	Path     string `json:"path"`                // worktree-relative, posix slashes
	Op       string `json:"op"`                  // create | update | delete
	Bytes    int64  `json:"bytes"`               // size of stashed content (0 for delete)
	OldHash  string `json:"old_hash"`            // pre-pull HEAD blob hash, "" if absent
	StashRef string `json:"stash_ref,omitempty"` // path under .changes.stash/, "" for delete
}
    StashEntry is one path captured by PullWithStash before the worktree reset;
    Op drives the restore (write vs re-delete).

type StashPathPending struct {
	Path string `json:"path"`
	Op   string `json:"op"`
}
    StashPathPending is one journal-pending path, declared locally so the git
    signature avoids importing journal types.

type StashedPullResult struct {
	Pull       *PullResult      `json:"pull"`
	Stashed    []string         `json:"stashed"`
	Restored   []string         `json:"restored"`
	AutoMerged []string         `json:"auto_merged"`
	Overridden []OverriddenPath `json:"overridden"`
}
    StashedPullResult is the outcome of PullWithStash: Restored re-applied
    cleanly, AutoMerged via recmerge, Overridden where pull won and the local
    change was dropped (with remote authorship captured).

    Policy: pull always wins on disk; auto-merge meta.json when recmerge
    reconciles, else drop the user's change. .changes.stash is always cleaned
    up; the Overridden list is the only signal that something was lost.

type Status struct {
	// Branch is the current local branch, empty when detached.
	Branch string `json:"branch"`
	// Tracking is the upstream ref (e.g. "refs/remotes/origin/main"), or "" if none.
	Tracking string `json:"tracking"`
	Detached bool   `json:"detached"`
	Clean    bool   `json:"clean"`
	Ahead    int    `json:"ahead"`
	// Behind reflects the last-known Tracking state; call Fetch first to refresh it.
	Behind int `json:"behind"`

	Modified   []string `json:"modified"`
	Untracked  []string `json:"untracked"`
	Staged     []string `json:"staged"`
	Deleted    []string `json:"deleted"`
	Renamed    []string `json:"renamed"`
	Conflicted []string `json:"conflicted"`
}
    Status is a JSON-friendly snapshot of a repository's working tree + HEAD
    position.

type Sysgit interface {
	Available() bool
	Fetch(workdir, remote string) error
	Push(workdir, remote string) (alreadyUpToDate bool, err error)
	Pull(workdir, remote string) (alreadyUpToDate bool, err error)
}
    Sysgit is the system-git transport for self-cloned mode; Available() gates
    dispatch so a missing binary falls back to go-git.



package sysgit // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/collaboration/git/sysgit"

Package sysgit shells out to the system `git` binary for network ops
(fetch/push/pull) in self-cloned mode, so Formidable honours the user's existing
credential helper instead of its own keychain PAT.

FUNCTIONS

func ErrNotAvailable() error
    ErrNotAvailable reports the not-installed case so callers can localize it
    without string matching.


TYPES

type Executor interface {
	LookPath(name string) (string, error)
	Run(workdir, name string, args []string) (stdout, stderr string, err error)
}
    Executor runs the git binary. Both stdout and stderr are captured because
    git splits its up-to-date messages between them: `git push` reports
    "Everything up-to-date" on stderr, `git pull` reports "Already up to date."
    on stdout.

type Runner struct {
	// Has unexported fields.
}
    Runner shells out to system git; construct once at startup, Available()
    stays stable for the process lifetime.

func NewRunner(log *slog.Logger) *Runner
    NewRunner detects the git binary on PATH; callers must check Available()
    before invoking an op.

func (r *Runner) Available() bool

func (r *Runner) Binary() string
    Binary returns the resolved git path, "" when not available.

func (r *Runner) Fetch(workdir, remote string) error
    Fetch runs `git fetch <remote>` inside workdir, folding stderr into the
    error and a warn log.

func (r *Runner) Pull(workdir, remote string) (alreadyUpToDate bool, err error)
    Pull runs `git pull <remote>`; alreadyUpToDate flips true on "Already up to
    date." (git emits it on stdout).

func (r *Runner) Push(workdir, remote string) (alreadyUpToDate bool, err error)
    Push runs `git push <remote>`; alreadyUpToDate flips true on "Everything
    up-to-date" (git emits it on stderr).



package recmerge // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/collaboration/recmerge"

Package recmerge implements structured 3-way merge for Formidable record files
(storage/<template>/*.meta.json). Leaf package: imports nothing else here,
no side effects.

Source of truth: github.com/petervdpas/GiGot/internal/formidable.
This is a hand-vendored copy (no build-time dependency on GiGot). Client and
server must produce byte-identical merged output for the same input triple,
so any merge-rule change must ship to BOTH repos in the same session; drift
is a correctness bug. Full spec: gigot's docs/design/structured-sync-api.md
§10.2-§10.3.

VARIABLES

var ErrMalformedRecord = errors.New("recmerge: malformed record")

FUNCTIONS

func IsRecordPath(p string) bool
    IsRecordPath reports whether p matches storage/<template>/<name>.meta.json
    (no traversal, not the images dir).

func UpdatedWinner(theirs, yours map[string]any) string
    UpdatedWinner returns "theirs" or "yours" by max(meta.updated.at); ties and
    unparseable values resolve to "yours" (stable). Accepts both the audit-block
    object and the legacy flat string form.


TYPES

type FieldConflict struct {
	Scope  string `json:"scope"`
	Key    string `json:"key"`
	Reason string `json:"reason,omitempty"`
}
    FieldConflict is one entry in a RecordConflict; Scope is always "meta" today
    (data fields never conflict under the uniform rule).

func MergeMeta(base, theirs, yours map[string]any) (map[string]any, []FieldConflict)
    MergeMeta applies gigot §10.2 for the meta map. A nil base (first-ever
    write) degrades immutability checks to "take whichever side has the value".
    The returned map is independent of all inputs.

type MergeResult struct {
	Merged   []byte
	Conflict *RecordConflict
}
    MergeResult is the outcome of a record-level merge; exactly one of Merged
    or Conflict is non-nil. Conflict is reserved for immutable-meta violations,
    which short-circuit the data merge.

func Merge(path string, base, theirs, yours Record) (MergeResult, error)
    Merge applies gigot §10.2 + §10.3: neither-changed keeps base,
    one-side-changed takes that side, both-changed-differently resolves by
    last-writer-wins on meta.updated. Missing keys compare as nil.

type Record struct {
	Meta map[string]any `json:"meta"`
	Data map[string]any `json:"data"`
}
    Record is the parsed form of a *.meta.json file; Meta and Data are generic
    maps (the merger treats each value as atomic).

func ParseRecord(raw []byte) (Record, error)
    ParseRecord decodes raw JSON into a Record; missing meta/data become empty
    maps, empty input returns an empty Record.

func (r Record) CanonicalJSON() ([]byte, error)
    CanonicalJSON re-serialises with map keys sorted at every depth (array
    order preserved). Byte-identical output across servers is load-bearing for
    mirror-sync and stable commit hashes.

type RecordConflict struct {
	Path           string          `json:"path"`
	CurrentVersion string          `json:"current_version,omitempty"`
	FieldConflicts []FieldConflict `json:"field_conflicts"`
}
    RecordConflict is the conflict body from gigot §10.6; today only
    immutable-meta violations on created/id/template.



package config // import "github.com/petervdpas/formidable2/internal/modules/config"

Package config owns the user configuration, boot profile, and the derived
Virtual File System (VFS) view of the on-disk Formidable data layout. Wails-only
- no HTTP handlers; raw config is too sensitive even for the loopback API.

The package is split across several files by concern:

    domain.go     Manager type, lifecycle (NewManager, Set*),
                  cache invalidation primitives.
    boot.go       .boot.json read/repair + active profile pointer.
    config_io.go  LoadUserConfig / UpdateUserConfig / persist / parse,
                  plus the JSON marshal helpers (writeJSON, syncJournal).
    vfs.go        Virtual File System view of the context folder
                  (templates + storage tree, per-template lookups).
    profiles.go   Profile management - switch / list / current,
                  import / export / delete + filename normalisation.

Package config owns the user configuration, boot profile, and the derived
Virtual File System (VFS) view of the on-disk Formidable data layout. Wails-only
- no HTTP handlers; raw config is too sensitive even for the loopback API.

CONSTANTS

const (
	ToastTimeoutMin     = 2
	ToastTimeoutMax     = 15
	ToastTimeoutDefault = 5

	// DecimalPrecision: how many decimals chart percentage labels show.
	// 0 = whole numbers (the historical look).
	DecimalPrecisionMin     = 0
	DecimalPrecisionMax     = 3
	DecimalPrecisionDefault = 0
)
    Numeric setting bounds enforced on load. The frontend's input min/max is
    the first line of defence; these clamps are the backend's safety net for
    user.json edited by hand, copied between versions, or written by future
    external tooling.


FUNCTIONS

func IsValidProfileFilename(name string) bool
    IsValidProfileFilename reports whether name is a syntactically valid profile
    filename: lowercase ASCII letters / digits / hyphens, ending in ".json".
    Source of truth for create + import paths.


TYPES

type BootConfig struct {
	ActiveProfile string `json:"active_profile"`
}
    BootConfig points at the active profile and is stored in config/.boot.json.

type Config struct {
	ProfileName          string        `json:"profile_name"`
	Theme                string        `json:"theme"`
	ShowPasteButtons     bool          `json:"show_paste_buttons"`
	UseExpressions       bool          `json:"use_expressions"`
	ShowMetaSection      bool          `json:"show_meta_section"`
	IoCollectionOnly     bool          `json:"io_collection_only"`
	LoopStateCollapsed   bool          `json:"loop_state_collapsed"`
	FieldStateCollapsed  bool          `json:"field_state_collapsed"`
	FontSize             int           `json:"font_size"`
	DevelopmentEnable    bool          `json:"development_enable"`
	LoggingEnabled       bool          `json:"logging_enabled"`
	EnablePlugins        bool          `json:"enable_plugins"`
	EnableFullTextSearch bool          `json:"enable_full_text_search"`
	UpdateCheck          bool          `json:"update_check"`
	ContextMode          string        `json:"context_mode"`
	ContextRibbon        string        `json:"context_ribbon"`
	ContextFolder        string        `json:"context_folder"`

	AuthorName           string        `json:"author_name"`
